## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard phase-space form of (non)linear oscillator equations. Typical structures combine a restoring force term depending on x, damping depending on v, and optional external/parametric forcing depending explicitly on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring force, conservative oscillator)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear spring + viscous damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Pendulum equation (with damping): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (nonlinear restoring from gravity, small-angle reduces to linear)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with periodic drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos under forcing)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (drag dominated at higher speeds)
- Nonlinear (cubic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (phenomenological amplitude-dependent damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation and limit cycle via state-dependent damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent pumping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (negative damping at small |v|, positive at large |v|)
- Liénard-type oscillator (general form): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) - (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (broad class generating stable limit cycles)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness, Mathieu-type behavior)
- Polynomial potential force expansion: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (higher-order restoring terms from a nonlinear potential)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force → dv_dt primarily a function of x with odd symmetry (e.g., -c * x, -c * sin(c * x), -c * x - c * x**3), with minimal direct dependence on v or t.
- Viscous dissipation → linear term -c * v; energy loss per cycle increases with amplitude when additional nonlinear damping terms like -c * v**3 or -c * v * Abs(v) appear.
- Geometric/pendulum nonlinearity → sin(c * x) structure; small-amplitude data often fits the linearized approximation dv_dt ≈ -c * x.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness → sign/magnitude of x**3 (and higher odd powers) controls amplitude-dependent frequency shifts and nonlinear resonance bending.
- Self-excited (limit-cycle) behavior → state-dependent damping such as (c0 - x**2) * v or (c0 - v**2) * v indicates negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- External periodic forcing → explicit cos(c * t) or sin(c * t) additive terms; typically produces steady-state response peaks and possible sub/super-harmonics.
- Parametric excitation → time-periodic modulation multiplying x (or v), e.g., (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x; associated with parametric resonance bands.
- Odd symmetry in phase space → many oscillators satisfy dv_dt(-x, -v, t) = -dv_dt(x, v, t); violations suggest asymmetric potentials or non-symmetric forcing.
- Model identifiability cue → if dv_dt correlates strongly with x but weakly with v, expect weak damping; if it correlates with v strongly, expect dominant dissipation or active pumping terms.
